RFC 7230, section 6.1\n//\n// Based on https://github.com/golang/go/blob/dc04f3ba1f25313bc9c97e728620206c235db9ee/src/net/http/httputil/reverseproxy.go#L411-L421\nfunc removeConnectionHeaders(h Hop-by-hop headers. These are removed when sent to the backend.\n// As of RFC 7230, hop-by-hop headers are required to appear in the\n// Connection header field. These are the headers defined by the\n// obsoleted RFC 2616 (section 13.5.1) and are used for backward\n// compatibility.\n//\n// Copied from https://github.com/golang/go/blob/dc04f3ba1f25313bc9c97e728620206c235db9ee/src/net/http/httputil/reverseproxy.go#L171-L186\nvar hopHeaders = []string{\n\t\"Connection\",\n\t\"Proxy-Connection\", // non-standard but still sent by libcurl and rejected by e.g. google\n\t\"Keep-Alive\",\n\t\"Proxy-Authenticate\",\n\t\"Proxy-Authorization\",\n\t\"Te\",      // canonicalized version of \"TE\"\n\t\"Trailer\", // not Trailers per URL above; https://www.rfc-editor.org/errata_search.php?eid=4522\n\t\"Transfer-Encoding\",\n\t\"Upgrade\",\n\t\"User-Agent\",\n}\n\n// removeHopByHopHeaders removes hop-by-hop headers. Especially\n// important is \"Connection\" because we want a persistent\n// connection, regardless of what the client sent to us.\n//\n// Based on https://github.com/golang/go/blob/dc04f3ba1f25313bc9c97e728620206c235db9ee/src/net/http/httputil/reverseproxy.go#L276-L281\nfunc removeHopByHopHeaders(h map[string][]string) {\n\tfor _, hh := range hopHeaders {\n\t\tfor k := range h {\n\t\t\tif hh == textproto.CanonicalMIMEHeaderKey(k) {\n\t\t\t\tdelete(h, k)\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc removeNonAllowedHeaders(h map[string][]string) {\n\tfor k := range h {\n\t\tif textproto.CanonicalMIMEHeaderKey(k) == setCookieHeaderName {\n\t\t\tdelete(h, k)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// ensureContentTypeHeader makes sure a content type always is returned in response.\nfunc ensureContentTypeHeader(res *backend.CallResourceResponse) {\n\tif res == nil {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tvar hasContentType bool\n\tfor k := range res.Headers {\n\t\tif textproto.CanonicalMIMEHeaderKey(k) == contentTypeHeaderName {\n\t\t\thasContentType = true\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif !hasContentType && res.Status != http.StatusNoContent {\n\t\tres.Headers[contentTypeHeaderName] = []string{defaultContentType}\n\t}\n}","stderr":"","interrupted":false,"isImage":false,"noOutputExpected":false}}

This function checks the `FlagQueryServiceRewrite` feature flag:\\n- If enabled, it rewrites requests to `/apis/query.grafana.app/v0alpha1/namespaces/{namespace}/query` and serves them via the Kubernetes API machinery (`clientConfigProvider.DirectlyServeHTTP`).\\n- Otherwise, it calls `QueryMetricsV2`, which binds the incoming HTTP body as a `dtos.MetricRequest` (defined in `pkg/api/dtos/models.go`), delegates to `queryDataService.QueryData` or `QueryDataNew`, and returns the response via `toJsonStreamingResponse` which streams JSON back to the client.\\n\\n## 2. It:\\n- `parseMetricRequest`: parses queries grouped by datasource UID, resolves datasource info (from cache or service), and builds `backend.DataQuery` objects.\\n- `handleQuerySingleDatasource`: for single-datasource queries, builds a `backend.QueryDataRequest`, retrieves the plugin context via `plugincontext.Provider.GetWithDataSource`, and dispatches to the `plugins.Client`.\\n- `executeConcurrentQueries`: for multi-datasource requests, fans out queries concurrently using `errgroup`.\\n- `handleExpressions`: routes expression queries through the expression service (`expr.Service.TransformData`).\\n- It supports two routing modes: single-tenant (direct plugin call) and query-service/multi-tenant (via `QSDatasourceClientBuilder` which calls the k8s query service API).\\n\\n**`pkg/services/query/models.go`** defines `parsedRequest` and `parsedQuery` (internal query parsing types).\\n**`pkg/services/query/errors.go`** defines typed errors for the query path.\\n\\n## 3. Kubernetes Query API (Alternative/New Path)\\n\\nWhen `FlagQueryService` or `FlagQueryServiceRewrite` is enabled, the query is handled by:\\n- **`pkg/registry/apis/query/register.go`**: `QueryAPIBuilder` + `RegisterAPIService` register the query API group with the Kubernetes API server.\\n- **`pkg/registry/apis/query/query.go`**: `queryREST.Connect` is the HTTP handler called by the apiserver. It binds the request as a `query.QueryDataRequest`, calls `handleQuery`, which rebuilds a `dtos.MetricRequest` and calls `service.QueryData` (the same core query service).\\n- **`pkg/registry/apis/query/client/plugin.go`**: `pluginClient.QueryData` performs access-control checks and dispatches to the internal `plugins.Client` with the datasource's plugin context.\\n- **`pkg/registry/apis/query/client/instance_provider.go`**: `singleTenantInstanceProvider` wires the single-tenant plugin client.\\n- **`pkg/registry/apis/query/clientapi/clientapi.go`**: Defines the `QueryDataClient`, `Instance`, and `InstanceProvider` interfaces.\\n- **`pkg/services/dsquerierclient/qs_datasource_client_builder.go`**: `QSDatasourceClientBuilder` interface and implementations that bridge between the query service and the datasource client.\\n\\n## 4. Plugin Backend Query Dispatch\\n\\n**`pkg/plugins/manager/client/client.go`**: The `Service.QueryData` method looks up the plugin by ID from the plugin registry, validates it is not decommissioned, and calls `p.QueryData`.\\n\\n**Plugin implementations:**\\n- **`pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/grpc_plugin.go`**: `grpcPlugin.QueryData` — dispatches to the gRPC client for external plugins.\\n- **`pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go`**: `ClientV2.QueryData` — converts the request to protobuf via `backend.ToProto().QueryDataRequest()`, sends it over gRPC, and converts the response back via `backend.FromProto().QueryDataResponse()`.\\n- **`pkg/plugins/backendplugin/coreplugin/core_plugin.go`**: `corePlugin.QueryData` — calls `QueryDataHandler.QueryData` directly for built-in plugins.\\n- **`pkg/plugins/ifaces.go`**: The `Client` interface (alias for `backend.Handler`) that all plugin client implementations must satisfy.\\n\\n## 5. Plugin Middleware Chain\\n\\n**`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/pluginsintegration.go`**: `CreateMiddlewares` + `NewMiddlewareHandler` assemble the middleware stack that wraps every plugin call:\\n1. `TracingMiddleware` (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/tracing_middleware.go`) — creates OpenTelemetry spans.\\n2. `MetricsMiddleware` (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/metrics_middleware.go`) — records Prometheus metrics (request count, duration, size).\\n3. `ContextualLoggerMiddleware` — contextual logging.\\n4. `TracingHeaderMiddleware` — propagates tracing headers.\\n5. `ClearAuthHeadersMiddleware` — clears sensitive headers.\\n6. `OAuthTokenMiddleware` — injects OAuth tokens.\\n7. `CookiesMiddleware` — forwards cookies.\\n8. `CachingMiddleware` (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/caching_middleware.go`) — cache hit/miss logic for query responses.\\n9. `ForwardIDMiddleware`, `UseAlertHeadersMiddleware`, `UserHeaderMiddleware`, `HTTPClientMiddleware`.\\n10. `ErrorSourceMiddleware` — classifies errors as plugin-source vs downstream.\\n\\n## 6.
